                    <td>7/19/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/roto-riteup-july-19-2017/">Roto Riteup: July 19, 2017</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=11752">Paul Sporer</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>

        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        
        
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Had it not been for Mike Trout, Bryce Harper's rookie season would have been a much bigger national story. While it was just one year, Harper is on track to be among some of the game's best players. His .352 wOBA was the sixth-highest figure by a 19-year-old ever. The good news is most of the players who produced similar value to Harper at that age saw a nice improvement on their offensive numbers the following season. He also emerged as an aggressive base-runner and a strong base stealer. The power, which is already good, should continue to develop, turning Harper into one of the best fantasy outfielders in the game. That could happen sooner than you might think, too. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Chris_Cwik">Chris Cwik</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Harper's rookie performance has already put him among the game's best. He's a strong candidate to improve next season, and could be one of the best fantasy outfielders.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It's hard to argue that Harper was a disappointment this year after posting strong weighted offense numbers, but injuries limited him to just under 500 plate appearances, and he failed to deliver that major breakout that many fantasy owners were hoping for. That said, all his skills took a step in the right direction, as his walk rate jumped, he made better contact, which led to a decline in his strikeout rate, and his isolated power moved up a smidge. His average fly ball and home run distance surged as well, pushing him up to the 20th-highest mark among all hitters. Still just 21, there is little doubt that Harper is going to develop into an elite hitter. It seems that the only thing holding him back at the moment is his health. (<a href="https://twitter.com/MikePodhorzer" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Various maladies hampered Harper's season, but he still improved upon his rookie 2012 campaign, displaying power, patience and speed. Coming off of offseason knee surgery, the only question mark pertains to his health, as the 21-year-old has the skills and pedigree to enjoy a monster season.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Injuries have derailed Harper’s performance in each of the last two seasons, but it’s tough to say he’s injury prone. Running full speed into a wall would set most people back, and there’s nothing fantasy owners can do about a torn ligament while sliding. His performance was solid, though took a step back after he showed a lot of promise in 2013. That’s likely due to Harper getting over his thumb and regaining his timing after missing so much time. When the playoffs started, Harper once again showed why he’s one of the most talented young players in baseball. The sky remains the limit for the 22-year-old. If he can put together a full season, there’s potential for a top-10 fantasy season. The injuries could push Harper down into the late second round, which would make him a steal if he finally puts it together. The talent is immense. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Chris_Cwik">Chris Cwik</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Injuries have interrupted the last two seasons for Harper. He remains immensely talented, and could put up top-10 fantasy numbers the year he finally plays 150 games.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>This is the kind of season we were all waiting for out of Harper. He led all of baseball in on base percentage and slugging percentage, while leading the National League in homers and runs. What exactly can he do for an encore? Well, we've only had one 50+ homer season in the last five years (Chris Davis, 53 in 2013) so there's that. There is also the fact that new Nationals manager Dusty Baker brought Davey Lopes on board to coach first base. He's known as something of a base-stealing guru and it wouldn't be shocking to see Harper start to run more. Remember, he stole 13 bases in his rookie season. He has just eight stolen bases in the last two seasons combined, but one of those was a 100-game injury-marred campaign. "But middle-of-the-lineup sluggers don't run!" There have been 11 seasons of 30+ HR/20+ SB in the last five years. Alex Rodriguez ran throughout his prime. Hell, we just saw Manny Machado go for 20 after going 10-for-17 in his first three seasons with two devastating knee injuries. Paul Goldschmidt has three 15+ SB seasons in the last four (the other was 109 games cut by injury). This write-up can't be completed without at least mentioning the career-highs in homers per fly balls (27%) and batting average on balls in play (.369) which could come back a little bit and cost him some homers and average, but he also had a near one to one strikeout to walk ratio and an absurd 41% hard contact rate (tied for fifth w/Goldschmidt) so it's not like he lucked his way into those career-high marks. Take him with the first pick of your draft. (<a href="http://thespguide.com/">Paul Sporer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The fact that you read this site means you likely already know how useless RBIs are as a measure of how good a player's season, but if you're still on the fence consider that the unanimous MVP had just 99. Maybe if he hadn't taken so many walks and hit better than .330, he could've gotten more... or at least that's what Reds fans constantly tell Joey Votto.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>From a certain point of view, Harper's 2016 wasn't quite as bad as you may think. He was one of only nine players to turn in a 20-20 season, and his league-leading 17.3 BB% was a boon to those in OBP leagues. Still, he clearly did not perform as the #2 fantasy player many drafted him as. Rumors swirled that Harper was playing through injury or, in the words of Scott Boras, other "limitations". Regardless of their credibility, Harper had a clear drop in power from his breakout season in 2015; his HR/FB rate was cut nearly in half, from 27.3% to 14.3% (a career low), and his rate of soft-hit balls jumped from 11.9% to 19.8% (a career high). Harper also saw a 5% drop in his line-drive rate, which may have contributed to his .264 BABIP and, in turn, his .243 average. The big question, of course, is: will Harper's 2017 be more like 2015 or 2016? There's certainly cause for hope: Harper's 2016 turn as an oft-walking speedster is evidence that he'll find ways to contribute even when his power isn't on, and it can't be forgotten that he's *still* only 24 years old -- younger than Kris Bryant or Mookie Betts. Still, "2015 with a few more steals" is Harper's reasonable upside for 2017, so drafting Harper outright expecting that level of performance will likely leave you disappointed. There will probably be someone at your draft who takes Harper too high -- i.e. in the top 5 -- but if you can pick him up near the end of the first round, you may still end up with one of the two best players in fantasy come season's end. (Brice Russ)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>After a breakout year in 2015, Harper took a major step back in power and average last season, though his resurgence in steals helped ease the pain a bit. Harper is one of the very few players in fantasy baseball with 40/20/.320 upside, but you definitely don't want to pay for that level of production at the draft -- target him near the end of the first if you can.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>

        }

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setPart(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi' || node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi') {

    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
